  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_11a48dac-c722-4a6c-be24-2e1769466a7a'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText7014043464909503593" style="display:none">Who is Alex Carruthers? That is the question Wicked fans have been asking for nearly six years. <i>Spellbound</i>, the fourth and seemingly final book in the Wicked series, originally published in 2003, left readers on the edge of their seats with a classic cliffhanger ending. But now, as new fans of the bind-up editions of the series begin to ask the same question, the true and final conclusion to the Wicked series will emerge. And all their questions will be answered in this heart-stopping, magical adventure about witches, destiny, and the beyond.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62634959" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1818464-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255191563p2/1818464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62634959?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/1818464-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62634959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4153208039432728895">OK,here is . . . if you read the finale I don't know that your life will be any better for it. If you skip it, I am sure you won't walk around with a hole in your soul. The first 4 books were so dark and complex, I was hoping the final would bring everything together including our star crossed lvoers. Well, the authors tossed in Christian issues and myths and ressurecting people . . . that honestly one character did not need to be resurrected. I suppose those things are fine if there is a real r</span>
  <span id="freeText4153208039432728895" style="display:none">OK,here is . . . if you read the finale I don't know that your life will be any better for it. If you skip it, I am sure you won't walk around with a hole in your soul. The first 4 books were so dark and complex, I was hoping the final would bring everything together including our star crossed lvoers. Well, the authors tossed in Christian issues and myths and ressurecting people . . . that honestly one character did not need to be resurrected. I suppose those things are fine if there is a real rational behind it . . . I guess tying Merlin's actions to his jeolousy about being overlooked . . . I don't know . . . it just seemed a bit overreaching. And then Holly ends up saving the day at the end . . .I am not sure how she was permitted to so when she was expresively told not to do so. Miraculously everyone converged on the same war sight with a quickness . . . I'm assuming portals were used (just not explained). I just got the feeling the authors wanted to through in some glits and sadness and wrap things up but too rushed . . . or something. I finished and just couldn't wrap my head around everything. But I am done with it . . . <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4153208039432728895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5558392725892384945"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398314899ra/9399184.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That's pretty much my reaction to this whole book. Not only is it crazy long, but it's also just plain crazy. A lot of things just didn't make sense, especially the whole Blind Justices of Olympus deus ex machina crap that just came out of nowhere.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407512154i/10732141.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then there was the final battle which had the male lead wearing a <i>cat suit</i>. <b>No, just no</b>. Men weren't ever meant to wear those. Ever. If Quinto can't pull it off, neither can anyone else.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407511945i/10732129.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The flashbacks to Medieval Times needed to be more straight forwar</span>
  <span id="freeText5558392725892384945" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398314899ra/9399184.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's pretty much my reaction to this whole book. Not only is it crazy long, but it's also just plain crazy. A lot of things just didn't make sense, especially the whole Blind Justices of Olympus deus ex machina crap that just came out of nowhere.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407512154i/10732141.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there was the final battle which had the male lead wearing a <i>cat suit</i>. <b>No, just no</b>. Men weren't ever meant to wear those. Ever. If Quinto can't pull it off, neither can anyone else.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407511945i/10732129.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The flashbacks to Medieval Times needed to be more straight forward. I mean, was the goddess supposed to be some giant or was that just unclear writing?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407512526i/10732190._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I can say I was kinda disappointed in how the series ended, especially coming from where it started. This book droned on and on and didn't really tie up everything. I know it was released years after the previous installment, but it reads like a haphazard first draft. And also the demon cat or whatever on the cover doesn't really tie into anything so it was an odd artistic choice.</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781416995784" href="/book/show/6985696-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136370020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17174104964674706975">Six years after the cliff-hanger ending of 'Spellbound', the authors complete the series with Resurrection. There is more bouncing about the globe (and through time) by various folk searching for other folk, more demons, more revelations, more fireballs, more death and destruction, and some rather dubious returns from the grave. The authors also wove into the story the olde English ballad, Scarborough Fair, which made me want to go burn my Simon & Garfunkle CD. Suffice to say it really didn't wo</span>
  <span id="freeText17174104964674706975" style="display:none">Six years after the cliff-hanger ending of 'Spellbound', the authors complete the series with Resurrection. There is more bouncing about the globe (and through time) by various folk searching for other folk, more demons, more revelations, more fireballs, more death and destruction, and some rather dubious returns from the grave. The authors also wove into the story the olde English ballad, Scarborough Fair, which made me want to go burn my Simon &amp; Garfunkle CD. Suffice to say it really didn't work well for me.<br /><br />The series as a whole was kind of like popcorn: no real substance but once you start eating it almost impossible to stop until the bucket is empty. I think if I had been reading them as a teen before I had any real life experience of magic and witchcraft/Wicca I would probably have been enthralled by them and wanted more. Plus, I did enjoy Charmed and similar shows and they can be easily as convoluted and daft. <br /><br />I was also pleased that the authors resisted the temptation to introduce vampires into the mix though there was a point I really thought they might. No, they've saved those for their new collaboration.<br /><br />So overall, they proved entertaining enough and I didn't feel too much outrage at the authors' rather skew-whiffed take on witchcraft and Wicca. .</span>
  <a data-text-id="17174104964674706975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188901928?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather Dalgarno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather Dalgarno" href="/user/show/5868539-heather-dalgarno">Heather Dalgarno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5868539-heather-dalgarno?shelf=young-adult-supernatural">young-adult-supernatural</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188901928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer28313046130886413">This book was awful and I was pretty relieved to have finished it, bringing to an end the 1000 page + saga.<br/><br/><br/><br/>I have said before that the previous books were badly written, and that some of the plot points were pretty confusing. In this book they throw time travel and teleportation into the mix and it's just impossible to follow in many places. It's been very badly edited and since this book is mainly action that's a big problem.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Story-wise this is the most exciting of all 5 of the books, with the m</span>
  <span id="freeText28313046130886413" style="display:none">This book was awful and I was pretty relieved to have finished it, bringing to an end the 1000 page + saga.<br /><br /><br /><br />I have said before that the previous books were badly written, and that some of the plot points were pretty confusing. In this book they throw time travel and teleportation into the mix and it's just impossible to follow in many places. It's been very badly edited and since this book is mainly action that's a big problem.<br /><br /><br /><br />Story-wise this is the most exciting of all 5 of the books, with the most interesting goings on, but this was not enough to save the book in my opinion. It seems as though the authors came up with an idea, but didn't think through how they would actually execute it. Either that or they both wrote their parts without consulting each other. A case in point is the whole central theme of the book - the war between the families of Cahors and Deveraux. It hadn't been explained properly in the first 4 books just why they were fighting. In this book we're told it's because of the Cahors massacre of the Deveraux following the marriage of Isabeau and Jean, that it's because a Moore warlock murdered an earlier Cahors-Deveraux couple and told each family that the other was responsible, that they were at war because the other covens had encouraged it to keep them from becoming too powerful, and finally that the God and Goddess themselves had pitted them against each other as part of a giant cosmic battle. Each explanation is presented in such a way that in the end you really don't know what to think, and not in that clever way that some books have where they leave the reader to make their own mind up, more like the authors had brainstrormed all these options and then accidentally written them all in.<br /><br /><br /><br />In the hands of a more competant author and a better editor this would have been a fantastic series. Sadly though the poor execution has ruined a great story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="28313046130886413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62164662" />
    <a title="The_Book_Queen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1954982-the-book-queen"><img alt="The_Book_Queen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233097321p2/1954982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62164662?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The_Book_Queen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The_Book_Queen" href="/user/show/1954982-the-book-queen">The_Book_Queen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=one-of-my-favorites">one-of-my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=teen-fantasy">teen-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1954982-the-book-queen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62164662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10859889441938288492">Ever since I read Wicked two years ago, I've been a fan of this series. It may not be every one's cup of tea, and the magic in these books are nothing like Harry Potter, quiet the opposite in fact, filled with darkness and evil, and you never quiet know which side everyone is on....But that's one of the things I enjoy so much about this series.<br/><br/>And Wicked: Resurrection was anything but a disappoint, a fitting conclusion to the series. After having the last two books leaving you hanging, wanting m</span>
  <span id="freeText10859889441938288492" style="display:none">Ever since I read Wicked two years ago, I've been a fan of this series. It may not be every one's cup of tea, and the magic in these books are nothing like Harry Potter, quiet the opposite in fact, filled with darkness and evil, and you never quiet know which side everyone is on....But that's one of the things I enjoy so much about this series.<br /><br />And Wicked: Resurrection was anything but a disappoint, a fitting conclusion to the series. After having the last two books leaving you hanging, wanting more, Holder and Viguie finally managed to wrap it all up nicely, leaving the reader satisfied. It may not have the traditional HEA (happily ever after), but this HEA matches the story and characters, and that's all that really matters, right? <br /><br />I don't wish to give out any spoilers, from any of the three books, so I won't go into deep details. However, I will say that Resurrection manages to keep you guessing until the very end, throwing out new twists and characters just when you think you've managed to figure it all out. <br /><br />Darkness and corruption is zeroing in on Amanda, Nicole and Holly, but with the right knowledge and by working together, only they (and Owen) can turn back the malicious Merlin from destroying the world and killing them. Yes, it may sound like 'just another save-the-world' kind of book, but if you read the series, starting with book one (very important for understanding and enjoying the series completely!), you'll soon find out that it's nothing like what you'd expect.<br /><br />And to top it all off, besides the demons and magic and darkness, oh my!, Wicked: Resurrection has a nice dose of romance in it as well, between three separate couples. They may not have the perfect connection, and they all go through some really hard times, what with having ghosts from the past possess them and what not, but in the end, they stay together. And to me, that's what makes a romance more believable-- face it, none of us will ever have a relationship that doesn't have a few problems along the way, speed bumps that make us wonder 'Is it even worth it?'. But in the end, if you can survive the trip, the conclusion is well worth it. <br /><br />4.5 STARS! Wicked: Resurrection is a stunning finale to a delicious fantasy series. I'll definitely be recommending this to friends and family, and anyone else whom I think would enjoy the darker elements in the book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10859889441938288492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

This isn’t going to be good. <br /><br />Oh no the Dr is in love with Kari, he’s going to use the resurrection stuff that brought the cats back on Kari. I just know. Stupid Dr. I feel bad for the cats though. <br /><br />Who is the Dr talking to? And what did she mean that Kari’s body hadn’t been recovered yet? She was killed at the Supreme Covens castle. How was her body not found?<br /><br />Nicole’s baby is named Owen. Now all we need is his dad to be reveled. <br /><br />Why did Pablo collapse, how did he know something was wrong with Philippe is he ok? <br /><br />Who is this Rose chick why do they keep added new characters!! Not the Supreme Covens smaller factions. I think I’m wrong bough cause Eve said that Holly and them have the Supreme Coven in the run. Philippe saved Anne-Louise maybe they can help each other to find Nicole again. <br /><br />So now Philippe has reason to believe that he’s Owen’s father. What’s the reason? Is Owen evil? Is he getting it from Nicole like Tommy and Amanda suggested, or is it the house or is his dad really nearby? Who is in the house asking Amanda for help?<br /><br />I can’t believe he brought Kari back to life. But why was she in Hell? And why does she act and look dead inside? Did something go wrong? A dragon. <br /><br />That was a...odd time for Tommy to ask Amanda to marry him but whatever works. <br /><br />What is going on with Amanda? And why don’t they just leave that stupid house. <br />I wonder why Amanda is dreaming but no one else is. <br /><br />What’s up with the demons going after Armand? Is the guy Armand is talking about the one that got dropped into the fissure that opened in his tent? Nope it’s not never mind. <br /><br />Who is this Dark One? <br /><br />A book of prophecy’s. And who is the voice in her head. <br /><br />It seems like the only one that doesn’t have a past life/ ancestor who is the in the present time is Amanda.<br /><br />Is Kari really back from the dead cause even she says he just made the dead-her- walk again. Why does she think Nicole could do it? Holly is more powerful. I feel bad that they are leaving Osiris, Hecate wants him? to come. <br /><br />I feel bad for Kari and the cats, they didn’t ask to die or be brought back to life.         <div class="reviewText stacked">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer546333015" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5959003883316850474">This review is going to be a little quick. But I stand by on what I said in the first two books. The only difference with this book is the way the explanation of the feud between the two families.<br/><br/>In the first four books we know that the Cahors massacred the Deveraux family after the marriage of Isabeau and Jean failed to produce a child for the Deveraux and failed to give the Cahors the secret of the Black Fire.<br/><br/>But in this book, it turns out that a warlock murdered an Cahors & Deveraux couple th</span>
  <span id="freeText5959003883316850474" style="display:none">This review is going to be a little quick. But I stand by on what I said in the first two books. The only difference with this book is the way the explanation of the feud between the two families.<br /><br />In the first four books we know that the Cahors massacred the Deveraux family after the marriage of Isabeau and Jean failed to produce a child for the Deveraux and failed to give the Cahors the secret of the Black Fire.<br /><br />But in this book, it turns out that a warlock murdered an Cahors &amp; Deveraux couple that was apparently already married earlier and told each family that the other killed the couple. Who also told them that they were at war because the other covens had wanted them to kill each other to keep them from becoming too powerful. <br /><br />I'm sorry but . . . really? We are going to go with a 'misunderstanding &amp; misinformed' story? Why? Wouldn't it be more interesting if they just hated each other because of their greed? <br /><br />I felt that this was a cop-out and this is just to make the families seem not as evil and cruel. Seriously? <br /><br />We also have this other part of the story dealing with the God and Goddess but I honestly didn't care about that. <br /><br />So the ending was a little disappointing but other than that . . . meh. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6726316875862086288">The end of the feud is here. With our cast of characters spread across the globe, all working toward the end, it's up to fate if they win or lose this battle.<br/><br/>For Holly, she's with Alex and the Temple of Air fleshing out covens of warlocks and defeating them all. Alex still wants to be in thrall with her, and Holly is still reluctant because of her love for Jer. Armand and Pablo are still with her, but both are uneasy in this new alliance.<br/><br/>For Amanda and Nicole, they have taken up residence in the</span>
  <span id="freeText6726316875862086288" style="display:none">The end of the feud is here. With our cast of characters spread across the globe, all working toward the end, it's up to fate if they win or lose this battle.<br /><br />For Holly, she's with Alex and the Temple of Air fleshing out covens of warlocks and defeating them all. Alex still wants to be in thrall with her, and Holly is still reluctant because of her love for Jer. Armand and Pablo are still with her, but both are uneasy in this new alliance.<br /><br />For Amanda and Nicole, they have taken up residence in the Moore estate, that is rightfully Nicole's as Justin's widow. Trying to raise her son, Owen, Nicole has taken to motherhood but something is still not right. Amanda feels the evil the house and when she finds a book of prophesies, one that specifically talks about Owen and how he will end the world, she and Nicole contemplate killing the baby but neither can do it.<br /><br />As the final battle draws near, the girls and their friends will pay the ultimate price for their survival and the survival of the world. Defeating the army of the dead that Merlin raises will be the death of some of them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6726316875862086288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3064671653&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3064671653" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5903667287336944528">I don't usually write reviews with spoilers, but this one definitely deserves to be an exception.<br/><br/>Going back, if you successfully forced yourself to read book one, congratulations! It was one of the most boring books ever and I just kept hoping it would get better and it just didn't. Book two was slightly better, but it still had issues. If you haven't read book one, you can just skip it as all the important stuff is rehashed enough that you can understand what is going on without reading it. Boo</span>
  <span id="freeText5903667287336944528" style="display:none">I don't usually write reviews with spoilers, but this one definitely deserves to be an exception.<br /><br />Going back, if you successfully forced yourself to read book one, congratulations! It was one of the most boring books ever and I just kept hoping it would get better and it just didn't. Book two was slightly better, but it still had issues. If you haven't read book one, you can just skip it as all the important stuff is rehashed enough that you can understand what is going on without reading it. Book three was actually not bad and I sometimes did want to pick it up and read it. Book 4 was the best of the bunch and they really should have stopped there. So, on to THIS book...<br /><br />Resurrection...to start, why bring back Kari, no one liked her and she didn't really bring anything to this story. She would randomly say a word or two and then everyone would take what she said as gospel...and speaking of gospel, there was way too much Christianity in this. The Magi, Satan...and making Merlin the fourth Magi AND Satan?? What's up with that?? How could he even BE both of them?? The Merlin I've always heard about was a good wizard, not an evil warlock out to destroy the world. Bringing back Eli and Nicole at the end was nice and all, but not exactly realistic in the grand scheme of things. I mean, they can all do magic and conjure things, but there are some things that just can't be done. All the loose ends were pretty well tied up, Holly's dad, Richard's wife, Armand, Pablo, etc. Everyone got their happy ending after yet another epic final battle.<br /><br />All in all, if you're determined to read the series, skip book one. The rest of them aren't terrible. This one was kind of far removed from the others. I guess the characters had growth and development, but I didn't actually care about any of them, so it didn't matter to me. I was thoroughly underwhelmed by the end of this book and they should have stopped at book four. Good luck if you still decide to read all five of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5903667287336944528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_752987732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752987732" />
    <a title="vida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12349846-vida"><img alt="vida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562535559p2/12349846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752987732?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="vida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="vida" href="/user/show/12349846-vida">vida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=overwhelming">overwhelming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=final-in-series">final-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=question-mark">question-mark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=left-me-in-awe">left-me-in-awe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12349846-vida?shelf=what-a-cast">what-a-cast</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752987732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer855800704551995873">This is the second time I've read this book, and I feel absolutely burned out. <br/><br/>Not to say that I did not enjoy the series. Not in the least. I love this series--at least in the sense that I could read it again and again and stay engaged, although I'll admit it doesn't appeal to a wide audience at all--and not many people seem to know it or like it much. I bought <i>Wicked: Witch and Curse</i> from Barnes and Noble a few years ago and was shocked, at first. It was nothing like what the blurb on the back</span>
  <span id="freeText855800704551995873" style="display:none">This is the second time I've read this book, and I feel absolutely burned out. <br /><br />Not to say that I did not enjoy the series. Not in the least. I love this series--at least in the sense that I could read it again and again and stay engaged, although I'll admit it doesn't appeal to a wide audience at all--and not many people seem to know it or like it much. I bought <i>Wicked: Witch and Curse</i> from Barnes and Noble a few years ago and was shocked, at first. It was nothing like what the blurb on the back had me imagine. I was expecting the usual YA teenage romance, and some cheesy magical nonsense. <br /><br />Oh. My. Goddess.<br /><br />I was wrong. <br /><br />The book was so dark and full of things I almost couldn't comprehend. I didn't know how to feel about it at first. I spent a few months with Wicked simmering in the back of my mind before I had the courage to face it again. This time, though, I was ready, and with a new perspective, I found that I actually enjoyed the book. <br /><br />I've read all books in the series. I was at the library, browsing, and found <i>Resurrection</i> on the shelf. It had been at least a year since I read it last, so I decided to revisit it. And it was all nostalgia. <br /><br />I liked this series because of the authors' craft. The romantic scenes, the intense love between Isabeau and Jean, weren't cheesy. Okay, maybe they were to some people, but oddly, I didn't mind? I think the best way to describe it is that everything felt immediate and close to your face, if that makes any sense. It had a realness to it.<br /><br />Alas, I have digressed. <i>Resurrection</i> was...very intense. On the whole, it was acceptable. But...my favorite characters were killed off.<br /><br />I much preferred Philippe to Eli. I don't even know what Eli did to redeem himself...did he make any attempts? I honestly can't tell you. And the part when Nicole says something about Eli having gained a little part of Philippe? I was scratching my head at that.<br /><br />I was bored with Holly and Jer's arc. He's a perpetual pity party, we get it. I was annoyed that Holly insisted on loving him (though it was mostly due to Isabeau and Jean). That being said, I was very excited that most of this book was focused on the rest of the cast. Tommy and Amanda getting married? I was happy for them. And Richard impressed me. I didn't know he was a demon-killing machine. <br /><br />Kari was irritating at first. But then Holly butted in and I began to feel sympathetic. Kari really did love Jer, as Karienne loved Jean, but she was always cast aside for the Cahors witch. It really fascinated me how the authors entwined the story lines of characters from the past with their descendants. There seemed to be so many doppelgangers among the characters, and I liked watching history repeat itself. <br /><br />The epic battle was what confused me. I reread it several times. To my understanding, the dark wizard "Myrddin" (Merlin) was released from his incarceration - because he knocked up Nicole and wanted to see his son - and...everyone was planning to destroy him? That's why there was a war? Anyway, it turns out that the Horned God and the Goddess interfere and just go killing people on their own sides. Then the Blind Justices - which recruit Holly - banish them. Does that mean the God and Goddess no longer exist? And how is it, again, that Holly is a Deveraux? She's still a Cahors, right? I thought that she was a descendant of Karienne, but I'm so beyond comprehension right now. Fantasme (the child whose names means "falcon") is Merlin's son? What? My head is spinning. <br /><br />The deaths of some characters could've been overlooked if you didn't have your full attention invested in the book. I almost missed the paragraph where it mentioned that Sasha was gone. I don't remember how she died...but apparently, she is. Dr. Temar, I don't know. Was he even necessary? Why was Kari brought back? Or Hecate? Oh, yeah, that reminds me: where's Hecate after the near-apocalypse is over?<br /><br />These things aside, the scene with Pablo and Richard was unexpectedly poignant. I still loathe Eli, but whatever. Holly and Jer are still in the "Forever Time". Everyone's gonna get married, Eve has a boyfriend AND a long-lost twin sister, and time is fixed and healed and perfected and nothing will ever go wrong again. <br /><br />Until Holly kills Jer and starts the whole thing over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="855800704551995873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167087321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167087321" />
    <a title="Marissa Novels On The Run" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3794407-marissa-novels-on-the-run"><img alt="Marissa Novels On The Run" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350051210p2/3794407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167087321?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marissa Novels On The Run" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marissa Novels On The Run" href="/user/show/3794407-marissa-novels-on-the-run">Marissa Novels On The Run</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167087321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13350573805845664106">WOW!!! This was a very impressive series from Nancy & Debbie. They have certainly initiated me into a wider and more knowledgeable world of witches and warlocks. They gave me understanding of the world of Covens that I had not read before. Nancy & Debbie also delved on the more dark side of witchcraft in this series....It was refreshing to read a lead character dealing "with the devil" in order to save her own coven - bit by bit selling of parts of her soul each time. Though don't be fooled.....</span>
  <span id="freeText13350573805845664106" style="display:none">WOW!!! This was a very impressive series from Nancy &amp; Debbie. They have certainly initiated me into a wider and more knowledgeable world of witches and warlocks. They gave me understanding of the world of Covens that I had not read before. Nancy &amp; Debbie also delved on the more dark side of witchcraft in this series....It was refreshing to read a lead character dealing "with the devil" in order to save her own coven - bit by bit selling of parts of her soul each time. Though don't be fooled.....the dark side isn't always made up of evil beings - sometimes dedication to those in white comes at a price!<br /><br />Holly Cather's is our leading lassie! She didn't know she was a witch - let a lone one of the potentially most powerful ever. Naive to begin with.. Holly slowly evolves into a force to be reckoned with - but as I said above....it comes at a price. Thrust into the top position within the coven Holly doesn't get a users manual or workplace practice guide - she has to think quick on the spot and after a few pleads with the almighty Goddess....she realises that each time she receives assistance to save the lives of her coven members.....she loses a part of her soul.....or a loved one. To top it off, poor Holly is the vessel that her long deadish ancestor Isabeau shows up in.<br /><br />Jer (Jeraud) Deveraux.....Holly's possible love interest. He's from the opposing family and he's a warlock. Jer has a connection with Holly from the minute they meet. His family have been waring with Holly's family (originally known as the Cahors) for generations. An accident happens in the series (ok one of many!!) and regardless of it's outcome - I still see him as hotly handsome. He's a bad, bad boy and has the added affliction of being the Deveraux that his ancestor Jean channels through.<br /><br />Within the story of Jer and Holly also resides the recurring story of the tortured love between Jean de Deveraux and Isabeau Cahors which started centuries ago. They vowed on their own deaths to kill the other so they may be free. They burden Jer and Holly with this continuing saga - they love each other and hate each other at the same time - their desire to fulfill their own dying wish becomes so overpowering that Jer and Holly must fight through Jean and Isabeau to find their own feelings.<br /><br />Amanda and Nicole Anderson are Holly's cousins that she is to live with upon the death of her parents. They are twins with a difference. One the popular rebel and the other fairly straight-laced and average. They have a dislike and love for each other which is tested over the series time and again. In the beginning they are also not fully aware of the witching abilities.<br /><br />Eli Deveraux = BAD BAD BAD BAD right to down to the core..... he's the creation of his ultra evil father Michael Deveraux. Together they are hell bent on extinguishing the Cahors Witches (Holly, Amanda and Nicole). Eli will surprise you - and his evilness will not dissappoint at times either. He is Nicole Anderson's rebel boyfriend (the one to annoy the parents with!). Micheal is just so evil words fail me to describe how utterly horrible a being he is. He will stop at NOTHING to kill Holly.<br /><br />There are so many characters within the 5 books - all of which play pivotal roles......you don't often find minor characters being so prominent within a story that they just about become lead characters in their own right.<br /><br />I had an awesome action packed, dark magic ride with The Wicked Series. The fight between good and evil is certainly not what it is always depicted in most novels and Nancy and Debbie have given us a roller coaster series filled with despair, grief, joy, happiness, suspense, action and shock!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13350573805845664106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78665199" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78665199" />
    <a title="Leann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2522741-leann"><img alt="Leann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546753337p2/2522741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78665199?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leann" href="/user/show/2522741-leann">Leann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2522741-leann?shelf=printed-book">printed-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2522741-leann?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78665199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18209189423916955597">Resurrection is the fifth novel in the Wicked series. Check out my reviews on Wicked and Wicked 2.<br/><br/>Resurrection was a satisfying ending to the Wicked series. At the end of the last novel Spellbound, I was left breathless, and shocked, at the cliffhanger. So I was even more surprised when the cliffhanger wasn't even acknowledged until about 90 pages in, and even then, the same character was still the only one with that knowledge.<br/><br/>More surprises fill the pages, as well as prophecies regarding the Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText18209189423916955597" style="display:none">Resurrection is the fifth novel in the Wicked series. Check out my reviews on Wicked and Wicked 2.<br /><br />Resurrection was a satisfying ending to the Wicked series. At the end of the last novel Spellbound, I was left breathless, and shocked, at the cliffhanger. So I was even more surprised when the cliffhanger wasn't even acknowledged until about 90 pages in, and even then, the same character was still the only one with that knowledge.<br /><br />More surprises fill the pages, as well as prophecies regarding the Cather's girls that seem to be eerily true. It's difficult for me to talk about one of my favorite eerie parts, without making this a spoiler filled review, but one of the newest characters was definitely creepy.<br /><br />The characters were fun to read about still, and I found many of them more likable. I really enjoyed Amanda's discoveries in the novel, regarding Merlin's prophecies. Richard completely kicks butt in this book, as usual, and even gets a little something back to help him get over the past. I was surprised to find myself favoring Amanda over Nicole, because Nicole was my favorite character in the past books.<br /><br />It was nice to see the characters all finally deal with issues they've avoided and ran away from.<br /><br />Highlights: I was just continually shocked as the pages turned. It seemed like there was so much to the story that had never really been revealed. It seemed like this novel was easier to read, maybe because I finally got used to all the POV changes.<br /><br />Lowlights: The ending fight scene was a little disappointing at how quickly and easily it ended. I also disliked how many times characters seemed to die (and some would be resurrected). It was also a bit odd how many of the characters were reincarnations of ancestors. I also felt like a few things about some characters were not clearly wrapped up.<br /><br />As a whole, Resurrection was one of the easiest to understand. My favorite still remains to be Spellbound, but Resurrection was a good follow up and a great ending to an interesting series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18209189423916955597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2117309676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2117309676" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7105731-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516201606p2/7105731.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117309676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3950873209608603661">Resurrection ends the Wicked series with a bang. Alex Carruthers is leading the coven to kill off the remaining members of the evil coven, with Holly in tow. Nicole and her family discover she is the heiress to the Moore mansion and fortune. The main question throughout the book is will they find each other again and will they finally defeat evil. A satisfying ending to a good series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OPMyLN2ZTIQ62Cu+xlgIC76jOmIaC8YeQxXtoN6E9h+sw9XrOdQCwHjs3nuAEQgvZLB687qYmAusJtk8Av80ig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16747689927808677486">Nancy Holder, New York Times Bestselling author of the WICKED Series, has just published CRUSADE - the first book in a new vampire series cowritten with Debbie Viguie. The last book her her Possession series is set to release in March 2011.<br/><br/>Nancy was born in Los Altos, California, and her family settled for a time in Walnut Creek. Her father, who taught at Stanford, joined the navy and the family t</span>
  <span id="freeText16747689927808677486" style="display:none">Nancy Holder, New York Times Bestselling author of the WICKED Series, has just published CRUSADE - the first book in a new vampire series cowritten with Debbie Viguie. The last book her her Possession series is set to release in March 2011.<br /><br />Nancy was born in Los Altos, California, and her family settled for a time in Walnut Creek. Her father, who taught at Stanford, joined the navy and the family traveled throughout California and lived in Japan for three years. When she was sixteen, she dropped out of high school to become a ballet dancer in Cologne, Germany, and later relocated to Frankfurt Am Main.<br /><br />Eventually she returned to California and graduated summa cum laude from the University of California at San Diego with a degree in Communications. Soon after, she began to write; her first sale was a young adult romance novel titled Teach Me to Love.<br /><br />Nancy’s work has appeared on the New York Times, USA Today, LA Times, amazon.com, LOCUS, and other bestseller lists. A four-time winner of the Bram Stoker Award from the Horror Writers Association, she has also received accolades from the American Library Association, the American Reading Association, the New York Public Library, and Romantic Times.<br /><br />She and Debbie Viguié co-authored the New York Times bestselling series Wicked for Simon and Schuster. They have continued their collaboration with the Crusade series, also for Simon and Schuster, and the Wolf Springs Chronicles for Delacorte (2011.) She is also the author of the young adult horror series Possessions for Razorbill. She has sold many novels and book projects set in the Buffy the Vampire Slayer, Angel, Saving Grace, Hellboy, and Smallville universes.<br /><br />She has sold approximately two hundred short stories and essays on writing and popular culture. Her anthology, Outsiders, co-edited with Nancy Kilpatrick, was nominated for the Bram Stoker Award in 2005.<br /><br />She teaches in the Stonecoast MFA in Creative Writing Program, offered through the University of Southern Maine. She has previously taught at UCSD and has served on the Clarion Board of Directors.<br /><br />She lives in San Diego, California, with her daughter Belle, their two Corgis, Panda and Tater; and their cats, David and Kittnen Snow. She and Belle are active in Girl Scouts and dog obedience training.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16747689927808677486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

But sorrow and grief soon give way to bewildered fascination as one by one, strange incidents begin to occur. Such as the fact that any desire Holly whispers to her cat seems to come true.
